5 Discussion
environmental impacts are primarily connected to the production of these ancillary
chemicals.
Figure 5.3 shows the results for the recycling technology employed to recycle the
blended fibre composed of 50% polyester and 50% cotton. It is mainly based on the
Lyocell process, which is a thermal procedure, and indeed, the heat is the major con-
tributor to the impact score of all the impact categories. The NMMO production,
the solvent used in the process, plays a worthwhile role in the human health cancer
effect, the terrestrial ecotoxicity and the depletion of abiotic resources - elements im-
pact categories while the contribution of water consumption is not negligible for the
climate change, the ionising radiation and the depletion of abiotic resources - fossil
impact categories.
The best-case scenario was conceived to evaluate the hypothesis of all the fibres
ideally source segregated and recycled simultaneously, and how suggested by the name
it was expected to be the preferable option for the management of industrial textile
waste. As evidenced in section 4.1 in the table reporting the normalised results, the
best case is not presenting the best score in the majority of the impact categories. The
contribution analysis shows that the impacts of the best case scenario mostly arise
from the polyester recycling technology, which is not levelled by the other recycling
scenarios.
5.2
Interpretation
The environmental performances for the baseline scenarios, modelled based on the
current industrial textile waste management system, were found to be comparable.
Nevertheless, the presence of impurities in the input waste stream is connected with
higher impact scores especially in landfill modules, because of the presence of an or-
ganic fraction which once landfilled undergoes biodegradation with the consequential
production of methane.
The best case scenario and thus, the simultaneous treatment of the textile fibres
are associated with relevant environmental burdens, and it is not an environmentally
preferable solution. It may be more valuable and advantageous to aim attention at the
recycling of those pre-consumer textile waste fractions which can potentially provide
benefits to the environment, rather than focus efforts on separately collecting each
single fibres to treat them. The polyester recycling technology is the worst among the
scenarios analysed since it has the highest impact scores in all the categories analysed
in the life cycle assessment. On the other hand, it is not straightforward to identify
which is the technology with the best performances. The 50% polyester and 50%
cotton scenario has the most significant benefits for climate change, photochemical
ozone formation and for the depletion of abiotic resources, fossil and eventually it has
negative scores in all the other categories. Generally, once excluded the best case,
the cotton scenario is the one performing better, and as a matter of fact, its recycling
technology gets the best scores in ten out of fourteen impact categories. Although
nylon recycling is not the scenario with the best performance in any of the categories,
==PAGE:73==
5.2 Interpretation
65
it is consistent to highlights that this scenario generates damages to the environment
only to the impact categories of the ozone depletion, human health non-cancer effects
and the ionising radiations.
Excluded the polyester scenario, all the recycling scenarios present negative im-
pact scores and thus environmental benefits in all the categories, representing a better
option in comparison to the current waste management system. The process contri-
bution analysis showed that the environmental benefits are mainly due to the virgin
substitution process in reason of the avoided impacts related to the avoided pro-
duction of virgin materials while the environmental burdens are associated with the
recycling technologies themselves. The electricity consumption and the virgin cotton
substitution processes are the main contributors to the impact scores in the cotton
scenario while for the nylon scenario alongside with the collection and the virgin
substitution processes also the electricity, the inert filler and water consumption in
the recycling process play a key role. The impact scores in the polyester scenario
are defined primarily by the recycling technology and specifically by the methanol
and toluene used as the solvent. Finally, the environmental performance of the 50%
polyester and 50% cotton scenario are controlled by the avoided production of both
cotton and polyester as much as the thermal energy, the water and the solvent needed
for the Lyocell process.
The results of the contribution analyses were the basis for the sensitivity and
the uncertainties analysis. In the baseline scenarios, the parameters expressing the
sorting facility was found to be the most sensitive with the highest sensitivity ratio
in all the impact categories. The electricity substitution ratio, the electricity for the
sorting facility and collection fuel consumption are influential factors for the systems.
The contribution analysis for the uncertainty of both scenarios leads to the same
conclusions. The collection (coll) and the sorting efficiency (sort_eff) are the main
contributors to the total variance in each impact category investigated.
The perturbation analysis for the recycling scenarios was carried out testing
the parameters identified in the baselines scenarios and all the factors inserted in
EASETECH for the modelling of the different recycling technologies. All the scenar-
ios result to be sensitive to the efficiencies of the sorting, the spinning and the recycling
processes specific for each fibre and to the substitution ratio for the virgin products.
This common behaviour is due to the main fact that a change in those parameters is
correlated to a change in the waste streams amount. The cotton scenario is primar-
ily sensitive to the sorting efficiency, which is also the factors bringing the highest
share of uncertainty in the system. The parameters representing the efficiency in the
sorting, recycling and spinning processes are accountable for the remaining portion
of uncertainty. The nylon recycling scenario is sensitive to the parameters mentioned
above and additionally to the electricity consumption in the recycling process, which
it is interesting to observe was identified as the most impactful factor in the contri-
bution analysis. The results of the uncertainty contribution analysis report that the
virgin substitution ratio is the main responsible for the scenario uncertainty in eleven
out of fourteen impact category and it is also the process associated to the highest
==PAGE:74==
66
5 Discussion
benefits for the environment. The polyester scenario is sensitive to the efficiency of
the sorting process and to the amount of methanol required for the DMT production,
which is the first step in the recycling of polyester. Moreover, it is relevant to men-
tion that the system is also influenced by the amount of toluene, which is the other
solvent employed in the first phase of the recycling process. The uncertainty results
are coherent to demonstrate that those are the most influential and uncertain param-
eters in the model. The 50% polyester and 50% cotton scenario has environmental
credits because of the avoiding production of both virgin cotton and polyester and
negative impacts associated with the consumption of thermal energy to carry out the
recycling process and with the consumption of NMMO and water. The system is
primarily sensitive to the efficiency for the sorting, the recycling and the spinning
processes, although the highest uncertainties are due to only the cotton sorting effi-
ciency and cotton substitution ratio. The results of the perturbation ad uncertainties
analyses spot that the factors towards which the systems are most sensitive are also
the one responsible for the highest share of the scenario uncertainty. These results,
coupled with those of the contribution analysis allow identifying for each scenario the
parameters affecting the environmental performance for the management of the end
of life of the different fibres within the industrial textile waste stream.
The sensitivity analysis was concluded performing a scenario analysis in which the
marginal technologies for the production of electricity and heat were modified. All
the scenarios result to be sensitive in changes in the electricity, while the analysis for
the heating scenario and the scenario in which are changed simultaneously both the
technologies for heat and electricity resulted in being relevant only for the polyester
and 50% cotton and 50% polyester recycling scenarios. The results for the electricity
scenario analysis are particularly interesting since the baseline scenarios respond to
the change in the electricity technologies with lower impact scores since the saving
from the electricity substitution overcomes the negative scores due to the other pro-
cesses. On the other hand, for the recycling scenarios, the electricity change leads to
an increase in the impact score of all the impact categories. This results may suggest
that a change in the management system adopted for the pre-consumer textile waste
in Italy has to be made as the transition to renewable resources for the production
of electricity have as a consequence an increase in the burdens associated with the
baselines scenario and an enhancement in the benefits associated with the recycling.
Eventually, the transport analysis was performed because of the absence of recy-
cling plants in the geographical area of Italy and specifically Veneto. Therefore the
evaluation of the impacts associated with the distances that the fibres have to cover
between the sorting and the recycling facilities plays a key role in the case study.
The preliminary analysis conducted assumed a sorting efficiency of 90% for all the
fibres did not produce any outstanding results. The ranking between the recycling
scenarios was changing only applying distances of more than ten thousand kilome-
tres, which has no relevance. Nevertheless, the analysis was carried out again but
changing the sorting efficiency, and therefore modifying the waste flows intended for
each treatment facility. In this new asset, relevant distances were obtained for some
==PAGE:75==
5.2 Interpretation
67
impact categories demonstrating that relevance of the transport process. However,
there is no a straightforward method to define the distances that might be travelled,
and they need to be assessed each time a different configuration is adopted in the
waste management system and in particular whether are made changes in the sorting
efficiency.
==PAGE:76==
CHAPTER 6
Conclusion
The current waste management system implemented in Veneto for the industrial tex-
tile waste was investigated through the analysis of two baseline scenario differing in
the composition of the waste stream to evaluate the influence of the presence of con-
tamination in the textile waste. Additionally, four different scenarios were built up
to evaluate the environmental feasibility of the recycling technologies for the different
textile fibres in the waste stream. The analysis was concluded with a best-case sce-
nario conceived to test the hypothesis of all the textile fibres segregated at the source
and sorted to be recycled simultaneously.
The study resulted in the following conclusions:
• The current textile management represents a burden to the environment.
• The presence of impurities in the waste stream makes worse the environmental
performance of the current textile management system.
• The polyester scenario have the largest environmental impacts in all the cate-
gories investigated in the study.
• The recycling scenarios built up for cotton, nylon, and the blended fibre com-
posed of 50% cotton and 50% polyester are all generating benefits for the envi-
ronment.
• The best-case scenario where all fibres are ideally source segregated and recycled
separately do not present benefits for the environment.
• Waste management strategies focused on single textile waste fibres is advanta-
geous for cotton, nylon and the blended fibre composed of 50% cotton and 50%
polyester.
• The factor representing the efficiency of the sorting process is the most sensi-
tive in all the scenarios analysed. The systems are strongly influenced by the
amount of waste intended to each treatment facility, small changes in the sorting
efficiency lead to considerable changes in the environmental performances.
• The parameters influencing the most the sustainability of Cotton, Nylon and
50% Cotton and 50% Polyester scenarios are the factors representing the sorting
efficiency and the virgin substitution ratio.
==PAGE:77==
6 Conclusion
69
• The methanol and toluene consumptions are the parameters affecting the most
the sustainability of the Polyester Recycling scenario.
• Transport distances are playing a key role in the environmental performance of
the scenarios and are influenced by the efficiency of the sorting facility.
The results obtained depend on the quality of the data obtained in the literature
for textile recycling technologies. As indicated in the introduction, technologies in
this field are still at a developing stage and data in the literature may not be accu-
rate. Taking this into consideration and given the results, it is possible to conclude
that the current waste management system for textile waste is posing threats to the
environment and that an alternative has to be found. The source segregation ap-
pears not to be a beneficial solution for all the textile fibres, and therefore strategies
based on single textile fibres may be beneficial especially for cotton, nylon and for
the blended fibre 50% cotton and 50% polyester. Furthermore, the results highlight
the fundamental importance of the sorting process which has the strongest influence
on the sustainability of all the recycling scenario and which have a deep connection
with the impact associated with the transport process.
The complexity of the textile waste stream as the scarcity of information leads to
the need for further analyses which should be focused on the trade-off between im-
pact categories, on the research of more accurate data for the recycling technologies
for the different textile fibres. Since there are no recycling plants neither in Veneto
nor in Italy, future research should focus on assessing the impact associated with the
construction of these facilities and as consequences to define the optimal distances for
collection and transport.
==PAGE:78==
APPENDIX A
Appendix
A.1
Goal Definition
A.1.1
Intended Application
This study aims to evaluate the environmental performance of the current waste
management practise for industrial textile waste in the Italian region of Veneto and to
compare it with improved scenarios implementing recycling technologies for different
fibres. The outcome of the study is supposed to be used by the region of Veneto as
a guideline to improve the current management system for textile waste in terms of
environmental performance and through the implementation of recycling practices.
Furthermore, the results are expected to be useful for textile companies to define
efficient handling of their fibrous waste and therefore, to improve the sustainability
of their products.
A.1.2
Method Assumption and Impact Limitation
The study is limited by the area where it is applied. This work analyses the waste
stream generated and treated within the region of Veneto disregarding the production
of textile waste from other industrial sectors and the import from other regions. The
method chosen in EASETECH to carry out the life cycle impact assessment of the
scenarios is the ”ILCD recommended 2013 Prosuit Global NR w/o LT” which do not
adopt any spatial specificity and therefore the impact scores are calculated as they
could have arisen in any part of Europe.
A.1.3
Reasons for Carrying out the LCA Study and Decision
Context
The region of Veneto has no gained knowledge on life cycle concept for its industrial
textile waste management, and it has not conducted or commissioned an LCA study.
The objective of the study is to evaluate the current waste management system and to
propose alternatives, including the recycling of pre-consumer textile waste. Eventu-
ally, these results are expected to be used as a basis for the environmental assessment
of factors that influence the sustainability of textiles and their end of life. Therefore,
==PAGE:79==
A.1 Goal Definition
71
it is supposed to be used to support decision making. The potential changes that
may be implemented in the waste management system and eventually in textile prod-
ucts are going to influence the present system. The decision context is situated in
Situation ”B: meso/macro-level decision support”.
A.1.4
Target Audience
The intended users of this study are the supervisors, Dr. Valentina Bisinella, Dr.
Anders Damgaard and external reviewers with knowledge on LCA. Also, this project
will be of interest for the region of Veneto and specifically the office responsible for the
Environment and the textile and clothing industries interested in the improvement of
their products.
A.1.5
Comparative Studies to Be Disclosed to the Public
This study is not disclosed to the public.
A.1.6
Commissioner of the Study and Other Influential Actors
This LCA study is commissioned by the Technical University of Denmark (DTU).
The region of Veneto and the textile and clothing industries belonging to the textiles
districts of Treviso and Vicenza are expected to influence the outcome
==PAGE:80==
72
A Appendix
A.2
Scope Definition
A.2.1
Deliverables
The deliverables of this study are: (i) detailed life cycle model for the current indus-
trial textile waste management system in Veneto, (ii) detailed life cycle models for the
industrial textile waste recycle, (iii) life cycle impact assessment and interpretation
of the results for all the scenarios evaluated.
A.2.2
Function, Functional Unit and Reference Flow
LCA is an environmental assessment which focuses on functions first and, after that,
on the systems that are necessary to carry out these functions. The function of the
presented system is the collection, the sorting, the transportation and the treating
of industrial textile waste generated within the region of Veneto and collected from
private companies. The system must sufficiently handle the waste properly and treat
it to reduce its environmental burden. Additionally, the system must accomplish the
Italian and European legislation as defined by the Italian Legislative Decree 152/2006
(Environmental Protection Code) and the Waste Framework Directive (European
Commission, 2008).
The importance of defining the function is based on the fact that the study has
to be as transparent as possible and allow future comparisons.
It is essential to
define a functional unit, which provides the qualitative and quantitative aspects of
the function. The functional unit of this study is the management of pre-consumer
textile waste generated within the region of Veneto during the 2017/2018 year, in
accordance with the legislation mentioned above. The amount corresponding to this
statement is 33140 tonnes (ISPRA 2018), but the study is carried out adopting a
reference flow of 1 ton to allow the scale-up of the results to any amount of waste is
considered significant to evaluate. The composition of industrial waste generated in
Veneto was not available and therefore for the scope of this LCA has been assumed the
composition reported in Table A.1 based on a study case realized in Turkey (Barışçı
and Öncel 2014).

A.2.3
LCI Modelling and Handling of Multifunctional Processes
To identify the correct Life Cycle Inventory modelling framework to implement, it is
necessary to identify the multi-functionality of the system. A product or a system can
deliver primary functions which arise intentionally, and it also may deliver secondary
functions usually with low or no relevance for the final users Hauschild, Rosenbaum,
and Olsen 2018.
In the present study, the different treatment options for waste are multi-functional,
as their primary function is the handling of the waste while secondary functions are
arising during the process. Recycling processes lead to the substitution of virgin ma-
terials while avoiding the disposal of the waste. Also, the incineration reduces the
volume of the waste, and in the meantime, it produces energy in the form of both
heat and electricity. Landfilling results in the production of methane generated by
the presence of organic waste, and eventually, the anaerobic digestion leads to the
production of energy and digestates which may be used as substitutes for synthetic
fertilizers.
The LCI modelling framework for decision context B is consequential with system
expansion with the hierarchy accordingly with the ISO 14044 standard IS0 2006 and
the ILCD guidelines ILCD 2010. Multi-functionalities are addresses with system ex-
pansion, and therefore data are consequential when available, otherwise attributional
to the point of substitution (average data).
A.2.4
System Boundaries and Completeness Requirements
The system boundaries delineate the confines between the foreground system repre-
sented by the waste management system and the technosphere that is the surrounding
economy. For this study, two different system boundaries are defined. The first one
represented in Figure 3.2 displays the current waste management for industrial textile
==PAGE:84==
76
A Appendix
waste in Veneto while the second one pictured in Figure 3.3 shows the expanded and
improved waste management system which incorporate the recycling of textile fibres.
The dashed line represents the boundaries between foreground and background
systems, the boxes in the background system symbolize the inputs required for the
processes and their outputs and the dashed arrows represent the avoided production
of virgin materials and energy in the background system, while the arrows repre-
sent the waste flow. Figure A.1 represents the current waste management system
implemented in the region of Veneto for industrial textile waste. Once, the waste is
generated, private companies collect it and drive it to the sorting facility where 90%
of the waste flow is sent to the landfill and 10% to the energy recovery facility. The
methane produced in the landfill site is not recovered, but instead, it is burnt in flares.
On the other hand, in the incineration plant are produced electricity, heat, bottom
ash and fly ash. The electricity is recovered and fed in the grid while the heat is not
as there is not district heating in Veneto. The fly ashes are sold to companies for
”underground reutilization” in exhausted salt mines in Germany, the bottom ashes
are used to substitutes primary or secondary aggregates. Eventually, from bottom
ashes are also recovered metals like aluminium and iron. Figure A.2 Represents an
alternative waste management system which includes the recycling of textile waste.
The model has been built up as the previous one with one main change. In the sorting
facility, the textile fibres segregated at the source are separated and sent to the recy-
cling facility where are treated and spun to obtain a new fibre. The residues produced
during the process are sent to the energy recovery facility. Transport to each treat-
ment facility is included in both scenarios since it contributes to the environmental
impact of the whole waste management systems.

A.2 Scope Definition
79
A.2.5
Representativeness of LCI Data
A.2.5.1
Geographical Representativeness
The study is carried out for the region of Veneto in the north-east of Italy. Data
regarding the industrial textile waste are expected to be found for the geographical
area of interest, and whenever they are not available, data for the country of Italy
are considered representative. The technologies implemented for the landfilling and
the energy recovery of textiles are modelled with data from the facilities present on
the regional territory. The modelling of recycling technologies are expected to be
done with processes as much as possible geographically representative of Veneto, or
in case it is not possible with data for Italy and countries of south - centre Europe in
accordance with their climatic and technological similarity. The electricity and heat
used in the processes of the models are explicitly modelled for Italy, since the exact
mix of electricity sources within Veneto may not be available.
A.2.5.2
Time-related Representativeness
This study is considered to be representative for five years. The definition of a time
frame for the results is a crucial step for this LCA as waste management practises
and technologies are constantly evolving. So far, several recycling technologies are
available only in laboratory scale, and the procedures to scale them up for industrial
application are in development and may introduce new alternatives for the handling
of this waste stream.
Additionally, new waste policies and regulations are being
issued by national and European authorities leading to changes in the composition
and amount of waste generated as in the treatment systems implemented.
Also,
behavioural changes and the raised environmental awareness of industries have an
influence on the amount and composition of the generated waste.
A.2.5.3
Technological Representativeness
The technologies implemented for the treatment of industrial textile waste, as the
landfill and the waste to energy plant are modelled with data representative for the
region of Veneto. However, few recycling technologies are available in the global mar-
ket, and thus, there is no data representative for Veneto. For all the other processes,
data for Italy or other south - centre Europe countries are considered representative
in accordance with their climatic and technological similarities.
A.2.6
Basis for Impact Assessment
The impact categories evaluated in this study are: Climate Change (kg CO2-eq),
ozone depletion (kg CFC-11-eq), Human Toxicity (cancer and non-cancer effects,
CTUh), Particulate Matter (PM2.5-eq), Ionising Radiation (kBq U235-eq), Photo-
chemical Ozone Formation (kg NMVOC), Terrestrial Acidification (mol H+-eq), Ter-
==PAGE:88==
80
A Appendix
restrial Eutrophication (mol N-eq), Freshwater Eutrophication (kg P-eq), Marine
Eutrophication (kg N-eq), Freshwater Ecotoxicity (CTUe), Depletion of Fossil Abi-
otic Resources (MJ) and Depletion of Elements (kg antimony-eq) as recommended
by EC-JRC 2011.
The solid waste management systems are modelled with the EASETECH software
and adopting the method ”ILCD recommended 2013 Prosuit Global NR w/o LT” for
the LCIA. This method does not account for emissions that will occur in more than
100 years and the normalization references are based on Laurent et al. 2013.
A.2.7
Requirements for Comparative Studies
This LCA study is aimed for internal use only from the region of Veneto and textile
and clothing industries. Special requirements for comparative studies are demanded
whether the study and its results are disclosed to the public, and therefore, special
requirements are not necessarily fulfilled.
A.2.8
Critical Review Needs
A critical review is not needed as the LCA study is not disclosed to the public.
